It builds a normalized index of tar members by stripping trailing separators\n2. If tar archives store directories differently, lookups can fail\n3. The workaround was for a CPython tarfile bug that's been fixed\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nimport pytest\n\n# Add the ansible module path\nsys.path.insert(0, '/app/lib')\n\nfrom ansible.galaxy.collection import _extract_tar_dir\nfrom ansible.errors import AnsibleError\nfrom ansible.module_utils.common.text.converters import to_bytes, to_native\n\n\ndef create_tar_with_trailing_sep_dirs(tar_path):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a tar archive with directory entries that have trailing separators.\n\n    This simulates tar archives where directories are stored with trailing\n    separators in their member names, which is valid tar format but can\n    break the normalized cache lookup approach.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'w') as tar:\n        # Add a directory entry with a trailing separator\n        # This is the problematic case that the custom cache can't handle correctly\n        dir_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/lookup/')\n        dir_info.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        dir_info.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(dir_info)\n\n        # Add another directory with trailing separator\n        dir_info2 = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/modules/')\n        dir_info2.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        dir_info2.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(dir_info2)\n\n        # Add a file in one of the directories\n        import io\n        file_content = b'test file content'\n        file_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/modules/test.py')\n        file_info.size = len(file_content)\n        tar.addfile(file_info, io.BytesIO(file_content))\n\n\ndef create_tar_with_mixed_dir_formats(tar_path):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a tar archive with directory entries in mixed formats.\n\n    Some directories with trailing separators, some without.\n    This tests the robustness of the cache when dealing with inconsistent\n    directory member naming.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'w') as tar:\n        # Directory WITH trailing separator\n        dir_info1 = tarfile.TarInfo(name='roles/')\n        dir_info1.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        dir_info1.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(dir_info1)\n\n        # Directory WITHOUT trailing separator\n        dir_info2 = tarfile.TarInfo(name='library')\n        dir_info2.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        dir_info2.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(dir_info2)\n\n\ndef test_extract_tar_dir_with_trailing_separator_entries():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test extraction when tar has directory entries with trailing separators.\n\n    This reproduces the core issue: when tar archives store directories with\n    trailing separators, the normalized cache lookup becomes fragile.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar')\n        extract_dir = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'extracted')\n\n        # Create tar with trailing separator directories\n        create_tar_with_trailing_sep_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        # Open the tar and try to extract directories\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # Build the normalized cache like the collection code does\n            tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()\n            }\n\n            # List the cache to understand what's being stored\n            cache_keys = set(tar._ansible_normalized_cache.keys())\n\n            # List the actual member names\n            member_names = {m.name for m in tar.getmembers() if m.isdir()}\n\n            # The cache should have normalized names, but let's verify\n            # that the lookup works for various input formats\n\n            os.makedirs(extract_dir, exist_ok=True)\n\n            # Test 1: Extract a directory that's stored WITH trailing separator\n            # When FILES.json references it WITHOUT separator\n            try:\n                _extract_tar_dir(tar, 'plugins/lookup', to_bytes(extract_dir, errors='surrogate_or_strict'))\n                # If we get here, extraction succeeded\n                extracted_path = os.path.join(extract_dir, 'plugins', 'lookup')\n                assert os.path.isdir(extracted_path), \"Directory should have been created\"\n            except AnsibleError as e:\n                # This might fail if the cache doesn't have the entry\n                # This is the bug we're testing for\n                assert \"Unable to extract\" in str(e), f\"Unexpected error: {e}\"\n                pytest.skip(\"Known issue: directory with trailing separator in tar not found in cache\")\n\n\ndef test_extract_tar_dir_name_normalization_fragility():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test the fragility of name normalization in the custom cache.\n\n    The custom cache strips trailing separators from member names, but this\n    creates a fragile lookup mechanism where archive layout variations can\n    cause extraction to fail.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_mixed.tar')\n        extract_dir = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'extracted')\n\n        # Create tar with mixed directory formats\n        create_tar_with_mixed_dir_formats(tar_path)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # Build normalized cache\n            tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()\n            }\n\n            os.makedirs(extract_dir, exist_ok=True)\n\n            # Directories use the custom cache (fragile, was a workaround for CPython bug)\n4. The workaround was for https://bugs.python.org/issue47231\n5. It builds a private normalized-name index for directories only\n2. Files use the standard tarfile.getmember() API (reliable)\n3. Directories use the custom cache (fragile, was a workaround for CPython bug)\n4. The workaround was for https://bugs.python.org/issue47231\n5. Modern Python versions handle directory lookups correctly with getmember()\n6. The custom cache creates unnecessary complexity and failure points\n\nThe test demonstrates that:\n1. It builds a private normalized-name index for directories only\n2. Files use the standard tarfile.getmember() API (reliable)\n3. Directories use the custom cache (fragile, was a workaround for CPython bug)\n4. The workaround was for https://bugs.python.org/issue47231\n5. Run with: python3 -m pytest --timeout=60 /workspace/regression_test.py\n    pytest.main([__file__, '-v', '--tb=short'])","newString":"def test_fragile_cache_direct_comparison():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that directly compares the fragility of custom cache vs standard API.\n\n    This test creates a scenario where the custom cache and standard API\n    behave differently, demonstrating why the custom cache is fragile.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_comparison.tar')\n\n        # Create a tar with directories\n        create_tar_with_multiple_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # Try to extract a directory using the custom cache approach\n            tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()\n            }\n\n            # Method 1: Using custom cache (current code path for directories)\n            cache_member = None\n            dirname = 'plugins/lookup'\n            try:\n                cache_member = tar._ansible_normalized_cache[dirname]\n            except KeyError:\n                pytest.fail(f\"Cache lookup failed for {dirname}\")\n\n            # Method 2: Using standard API (what the code uses for files)\n            api_member = tar.getmember(dirname)\n\n            # Both should find the same member\n            assert cache_member is not None, \"Cache should have the member\"\n            assert api_member is not None, \"Standard API should have the member\"\n            assert cache_member.name == api_member.name, \"Both methods should find the same member\"\n\n            # The fragility is that if the cache-building code has a bug,\n            # or if tar archives are structured differently, the cache might\n            # fail to find entries that the standard API would find.\n            #\n            # Currently they work the same, but the custom cache creates\n            # unnecessary complexity and a single point of failure.\n\n\nif __name__ == '__main__':\n    # Run with: python3 -m pytest /workspace/regression_test.py\n    # Note: The --timeout flag requires pytest-timeout to be installed\n    pytest.main([__file__, '-v', '--tb=short'])","originalFile":"# -*- coding: utf-8 -*-\n# Copyright (c) 2025 Ansible Project\n# GNU General Public License v3.0+ (see COPYING or https://www.gnu.org/licenses/gpl-3.0.txt)\n\n\"\"\"\nRegression test for Galaxy collection tar directory extraction fragility.\n\nThis test demonstrates the issue where directory extraction fails for certain\narchive layouts due to the custom normalized cache approach used only for\ndirectories.\n\nIssue: https://github.com/ansible/ansible/issues/xxxxx\nThe custom _ansible_normalized_cache approach is fragile because:\n1. It builds a private normalized-name index for directories only\n2. Files use the standard tarfile.getmember() API (reliable)\n3. Directories use the custom cache (fragile, was a workaround for CPython bug)\n4. The workaround was for https://bugs.python.org/issue47231\n5. Modern Python versions handle directory lookups correctly with getmember()\n6. The custom cache creates unnecessary complexity and failure points\n\nThe test demonstrates that:\n1. The cache is built by stripping trailing separators from member names\n2. If the cache-building or lookup process fails, directories can't be extracted\n3. Files work fine because they use the standard API\n4. This creates a fragile mismatch in the extraction logic\n\"\"\"\n\nfrom __future__ import annotations\n\nimport json\nimport os\nimport sys\nimport tarfile\nimport tempfile\nimport pytest\n\n# Add the ansible module path\nsys.path.insert(0, '/app/lib')\n\nfrom ansible.galaxy.collection import _extract_tar_dir, _extract_tar_file\nfrom ansible.errors import AnsibleError\nfrom ansible.module_utils.common.text.converters import to_bytes, to_native\n\n\ndef create_tar_with_multiple_dirs(tar_path):\n    \"\"\"\n    Create a tar archive with multiple directory entries.\n\n    This is used to test the cache-based lookup for directories versus\n    the standard getmember() API for files.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'w') as tar:\n        # Add directory entries\n        dir_info1 = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/lookup')\n        dir_info1.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        dir_info1.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(dir_info1)\n\n        dir_info2 = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/modules')\n        dir_info2.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        dir_info2.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(dir_info2)\n\n        dir_info3 = tarfile.TarInfo(name='roles')\n        dir_info3.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n        dir_info3.mode = 0o755\n        tar.addfile(dir_info3)\n\n        # Add some files\n        import io\n        for filename in ['plugins/modules/test.py', 'plugins/lookup/debug.py', 'roles/myrole.yml']:\n            file_content = b'test content'\n            file_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name=filename)\n            file_info.size = len(file_content)\n            tar.addfile(file_info, io.BytesIO(file_content))\n\n\ndef test_custom_cache_bypassed_on_standard_api():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that demonstrates the fragility: directories use custom cache,\n    files use standard tarfile API.\n\n    This shows that files can be extracted reliably using getmember(),\n    but directories depend on the fragile custom cache implementation.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_collection.tar')\n        extract_dir = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'extracted')\n\n        # Create tar with directories and files\n        create_tar_with_multiple_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        os.makedirs(extract_dir, exist_ok=True)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # Build the custom normalized cache like collection code does\n            tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()\n            }\n\n            # Verify that the standard getmember() API works for directories\n            # (This is what was fixed in Python 3.11+)\n            dir_member = tar.getmember('plugins/lookup')\n            assert dir_member.isdir(), \"Should be able to get directory with getmember()\"\n\n            # Verify that the custom cache also has the entry\n            assert 'plugins/lookup' in tar._ansible_normalized_cache, \"Cache should have normalized directory name\"\n\n            # Both methods work on modern Python, but the code unnecessarily\n            # uses the custom cache for directories instead of the standard API\n\n\ndef test_cache_building_strips_separators():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that demonstrates how the custom cache strips trailing separators.\n\n    This is the core of the fragility: the cache normalizes names, creating\n    a layer of indirection that's unnecessary on modern Python versions.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_cache.tar')\n\n        # Create a simple tar with a directory\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'w') as tar:\n            dir_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='mydir')\n            dir_info.type = tarfile.DIRTYPE\n            dir_info.mode = 0o755\n            tar.addfile(dir_info)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # Show what happens when building the cache\n            members = tar.getmembers()\n            assert len(members) == 1\n\n            # The member's name in the tar\n            member = members[0]\n            print(f\"Original member name: {repr(member.name)}\")\n\n            # Build cache with normalization (stripping trailing separators)\n            cache = {m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()}\n\n            # The cache key is normalized\n            cache_keys = list(cache.keys())\n            print(f\"Cache keys: {cache_keys}\")\n\n            # Both should work, but the custom cache is an extra layer\n            assert member.name in cache, \"Member name should be in cache keys\"\n            assert tar.getmember(member.name) is not None, \"Standard API should find the member\"\n\n\ndef test_directory_extraction_uses_fragile_cache():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that demonstrates directory extraction relying on the fragile cache.\n\n    This shows that _extract_tar_dir uses the custom cache instead of the\n    standard tarfile API, creating a failure point.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_dir_extract.tar')\n        extract_dir = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'extracted')\n\n        # Create tar with directories\n        create_tar_with_multiple_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        os.makedirs(extract_dir, exist_ok=True)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # Setup the custom cache\n            tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()\n            }\n\n            # Extract a directory using the fragile cache approach\n            try:\n                _extract_tar_dir(tar, 'plugins/lookup', to_bytes(extract_dir, errors='surrogate_or_strict'))\n\n                # Verify it was created\n                extracted_path = os.path.join(extract_dir, 'plugins', 'lookup')\n                assert os.path.isdir(extracted_path), \"Directory should exist after extraction\"\n\n            except AnsibleError as e:\n                if \"Unable to extract\" in str(e):\n                    pytest.fail(\n                        f\"Failed to extract directory using custom cache: {e}\\n\"\n                        f\"This demonstrates the fragility of using a custom cache\\n\"\n                        f\"instead of the standard tarfile.getmember() API\"\n                    )\n                else:\n                    raise\n\n\ndef test_cache_lookup_for_missing_directory():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that demonstrates cache lookup failure when directory is missing.\n\n    If the tar archive doesn't have a directory entry that FILES.json expects,\n    the extraction will fail with \"Unable to extract\".\n    This demonstrates the fragility of the custom cache approach.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_missing.tar')\n        extract_dir = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'extracted')\n\n        # Create a tar with only files, no directory entry\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'w') as tar:\n            import io\n            # Add a file but NOT the directory entry\n            file_content = b'test content'\n            file_info = tarfile.TarInfo(name='plugins/lookup/test.py')\n            file_info.size = len(file_content)\n            tar.addfile(file_info, io.BytesIO(file_content))\n\n        os.makedirs(extract_dir, exist_ok=True)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # Build the custom cache\n            tar._ansible_normalized_cache = {\n                m.name.removesuffix(os.path.sep): m for m in tar.getmembers()\n            }\n\n            # Try to extract the 'plugins/lookup' directory\n            # But it's not in the tar (only the file is)\n            with pytest.raises(AnsibleError, match=\"Unable to extract\"):\n                _extract_tar_dir(tar, 'plugins/lookup', to_bytes(extract_dir, errors='surrogate_or_strict'))\n\n            # This demonstrates the fragility: if FILES.json lists a directory\n            # but the tar doesn't have an explicit directory entry, extraction fails.\n            # With the standard API, we'd have the same issue, but at least\n            # the code would be consistent between files and directories.\n\n\ndef test_cache_is_unnecessary_workaround():\n    \"\"\"\n    Test that demonstrates the custom cache is an unnecessary workaround.\n\n    On modern Python versions (3.11+), tarfile.getmember() works correctly\n    for directory lookups, making the custom cache workaround obsolete and\n    a source of fragility.\n    \"\"\"\n    with tempfile.TemporaryDirectory() as tmpdir:\n        tar_path = os.path.join(tmpdir, 'test_workaround.tar')\n\n        # Create tar with directories\n        create_tar_with_multiple_dirs(tar_path)\n\n        with tarfile.open(tar_path, 'r') as tar:\n            # Demonstrate that the standard API works for directories\n            for dir_name in ['plugins/lookup', 'plugins/modules', 'roles']:\n                try:\n                    # This is the standard API that works on modern Python\n                    member = tar.getmember(dir_name)\n                    assert member.isdir(), f\"{dir_name} should be a directory\"\n                except KeyError:\n                    pytest.fail(f\"Standard getmember() failed for directory {dir_name}\")\n\n            #
